## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The variables (x, v, t) with target dv_dt indicate a second-order ODE written as a first-order system for a (possibly driven/damped) nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = f(x, v, t). Common structures include restoring forces (often odd in x), damping terms (often odd in v), and external/parametric forcing terms periodic in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (linear restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * x (small-amplitude linear oscillations)
- Constant-acceleration bias: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 (equilibrium offset / constant forcing)
- Linear viscous damping + stiffness: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * x (damped harmonic oscillator)
- Driven linear oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * x + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (harmonic forcing at frequency c3)
- Nonlinear stiffness (Duffing, undriven): dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * x - c2 * x^3 (hardening/softening spring)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * x - c2 * x^3 + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance/chaos regimes)
- Cubic (nonlinear) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v^3 (velocity-dependent dissipation)
- Quadratic damping (drag-like): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (dissipation proportional to speed squared)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x^2) * v - c2 * x (self-excited oscillations / limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator (nonlinear damping in v): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * v - c2 * v^3 (alternative limit-cycle model)
- Pendulum-type restoring (nonlinear geometry): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(x) - c1 * v (large-angle oscillations with damping)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * v - (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) * x (Mathieu-type behavior)
- Conservative force from polynomial potential: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x^3 + c2 * x^5) (multi-well / anharmonic potential)
- State-dependent frequency (amplitude-dependent stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * (1 + c2 * x^2) * x (effective stiffness increases with |x|)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: conservative oscillators often have dv_dt as an odd function of x (e.g., -x, -sin(x), -x - x^3), indicating symmetric potentials about x=0.
- Damping signature: dissipative terms are typically odd in v (e.g., -v, -v^3, -v*Abs(v)) and reduce mechanical energy; their presence often shrinks oscillation amplitude unless counteracted by driving.
- Self-excitation/limit cycles: terms like (1 - c*x^2)*v imply negative damping at small |x| and positive damping at large |x|, producing stable finite-amplitude oscillations.
- Multi-stability: adding higher odd powers in x (x^3, x^5) can create multiple equilibria (double-well potentials), often leading to jump phenomena and hysteresis under forcing.
- Periodic forcing vs parametric forcing: additive cos(c*t) terms model external drive, while multiplicative cos(c*t)*x terms model stiffness modulation and can yield parametric resonance.
- Geometry-induced nonlinearity: sin(x) restoring indicates angular coordinate dynamics (pendulum-like) with frequency decreasing with amplitude compared to linear -x.
- Nonlinear dissipation regimes: switching from -v to -v*Abs(v) reflects laminar-to-turbulent drag behavior and produces faster decay at high speeds.
- Autonomous vs nonautonomous detection: if dv_dt can be expressed without explicit t dependence, the system is autonomous; explicit t terms often indicate driving/modulation and can enable quasiperiodic/chaotic responses.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO20)

GT: -alpha*v**c0 - beta*log(Abs(v) + c1) - c2*beta*v - mu*(c3 - v**c4)*v - omega0**c5*(gamma*Abs(v)**c6 + c7)*x
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed) is the concrete function
\[
-0.0441723\,v^3\;-\;0.3334811\,v(1-v^2)\;-\;1.2494748\,v\;-\;3.5822062\,x\,(0.0479282|v|^{1/3}+1)\;-\;0.6247374\log(|v|+1).
\]
Key structural facts:
- It contains **log(|v|+1)** (not log(1+exp(kv))).
- It contains an **x term multiplied by (1 + const·|v|^{1/3})**, i.e. **both** an \(x\) term and an \(x|v|^{1/3}\) term with linked coefficients.
- In \(v\)-only terms it has **only odd powers**: \(v\) and \(v^3\) (since \(-0.33348\,v(1-v^2)=-0.33348v+0.33348v^3\)), and **no** \(v|v|\) term.
- No \(t\)-dependence.

Below, “can match” means: by choosing candidate constants, the candidate can equal the GT for all real \(x,v,t\) (with \(x,v\) allowed negative; abs cannot be dropped).

---

### Candidates 1–13 (softplus log + polynomial/abs blocks)
All of 1–13 share the same fatal issue: the log term is of the form  
\(\log(c\exp(kv)+1)\) (“softplus”), which is **not** equal to \(\log(|v|+1)\) for all real \(v\) for any constants.  
Reason: \(\log(|v|+1)\) is even in \(v\); \(\log(c e^{kv}+1)\) is not even unless \(k=0\), but if \(k=0\) it becomes a constant \(\log(c+1)\), not \(\log(|v|+1)\). No other parameter choice can introduce \(|v|\) inside the log.

Additionally, many include \((c\cdot|v|+1)^4\) terms which expand to even powers of \(|v|\) (non-polynomial in \(v\) due to abs) and cannot be canceled to yield only \(v\) and \(v^3\) unless their coefficient is set to 0. But even if set to 0, the log mismatch remains.

- **1**: has softplus log; also has \((c5|v|+1)^4\) and separate \(x|v|^{1/3}\) term (good), but log kills equivalence.
- **2–13**: same softplus-log obstruction; some add extra \(t\)-dependent or \(x^3,x^5\) terms that must be zeroed, but log still prevents match.

**Conclusion: 1–13 cannot match GT.**

---

### Candidates 14–21 (exp(v) + x*log(|v|) but wrong log form)
These have \(x\cdot \log(c|v|+1)\) (log multiplied by \(x\)), whereas GT has \(\log(|v|+1)\) as a **standalone** term (independent of \(x\)). You cannot turn \(x\log(\cdot)\) into \(\log(\cdot)\) for all \(x\) unless the coefficient is 0, but then you lose the required standalone log term entirely.

They also include \(\exp(c v)\) terms which must be zeroed (set coefficient to 0) since GT has no exponentials in \(v\). Even after zeroing exponentials, the only log present is tied to \(x\), so you still cannot produce \(-0.6247\log(|v|+1)\).

- **14–21**: all fail because log is attached to \(x\) (and/or other non-GT structures).

**Conclusion: 14–21 cannot match GT.**

---

### Candidates 22–26 (rational in |v| + x*exp(t)*log(|v|))
These include \(x\exp(c t)\log(c|v|+1)\), again log is multiplied by \(x\) and also has \(t\)-dependence unless coefficient is 0. Setting that coefficient to 0 removes the log entirely, so cannot match GT’s standalone \(\log(|v|+1)\). They also have \((c4|v|+1)^{-3}\) rational terms not in GT (must be zeroed), but log issue remains.

**Conclusion: 22–26 cannot match GT.**

---

### Candidates 27–35 (fractions with (c1+|v|) and trig)
These are built from terms like \(x|v|/(c1+|v|)\), \(x/(c1+|v|)\), \(v/(c1+|v|)\), plus trig terms \(v\cos(\omega t)\) or \(x\sin(\omega t+\phi)\), etc. GT has:
- no denominators \(c1+|v|\),
- no trig/time dependence,
- and crucially has a standalone \(\log(|v|+1)\).

You can zero trig coefficients to remove time dependence, but you still cannot generate \(\log(|v|+1)\) from rational functions of \(|v|\). Also, the \(x\)-dependence in GT is linear in \(x\) and \(x|v|^{1/3}\), not \(x/(c1+|v|)\) or \(x|v|/(c1+|v|)\).

**Conclusion: 27–35 cannot match GT.**

(Trigonometric phase shifts are irrelevant here because GT has no trig at all; the only way is setting trig amplitudes to 0.)

---

### Candidates 36–42 (exp(v) + (1+c|v|)^3 + v^c8 * x)
These have an \(x\cdot v^{c8}\) term (no absolute value). GT needs \(x|v|^{1/3}\) and also an \(x\) term. You might try \(c8=1/3\), but \(v^{1/3}\) over reals is not equal to \(|v|^{1/3}\) (it is odd, not even), and the problem statement requires strict handling of abs. So \(v^{1/3}x\) cannot equal \(|v|^{1/3}x\) globally.

They also include \(\exp(c v)\) and \((c|v|+1)^3\) terms not in GT (would need to be zeroed), but even if zeroed, the remaining \(x v^{c8}\) cannot become \(x|v|^{1/3}\).

Also none provide a standalone \(\log(|v|+1)\).

**Conclusion: 36–42 cannot match GT.**

---

### Candidates 43–50 (fractions with (c1+|v|), extra x-logs, etc.)
These again are rational-in-\(|v|\) constructions and/or include \(\log(c|x|+1)\cdot |v|\) (candidate 43), which is entirely different from GT’s \(\log(|v|+1)\). No candidate in 43–50 contains any \(\log(|v|+1)\) term at all, and rational terms cannot reproduce a logarithm globally.

Also, several include \(v|v|\) terms; GT has no \(v|v|\) term and you could set its coefficient to 0, but the missing standalone log remains fatal.

**Conclusion: 43–50 cannot match GT.**

---

## Overall conclusion
A necessary component of GT is the standalone term \(-0.6247374\log(|v|+1)\). None of the candidates contains a term that can be tuned to equal \(\log(|v|+1)\) for all real \(v\):
- candidates with logs use \(\log(c e^{kv}+1)\) (softplus) or \(x\log(c|v|+1)\) (log tied to \(x\)), or \(\log(c|x|+1)\) (wrong variable).
- candidates without logs cannot generate a logarithm from algebraic/rational/trig/exponential pieces by parameter choice.

Therefore no candidate can be made mathematically equivalent to the GT.

GT: -alpha*v**c0 - beta*log(Abs(v) + c1) - c2*beta*v - mu*(c3 - v**c4)*v - omega0**c5*(gamma*Abs(v)**c6 + c7)*x

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT numerical expression:**
`-0.0441723*v³ - 0.333481*v*(1 - v²) - 1.24947*v - 3.58221*x*(0.047928*|v|^(1/3) + 1) - 0.624737*log(|v| + 1)`

Let me expand this:
- `-0.0441723*v³`
- `-0.333481*v + 0.333481*v³`
- `-1.24947*v`
- `-3.58221*x - 3.58221*0.047928*x*|v|^(1/3)` = `-3.58221*x - 0.17166*x*|v|^(1/3)`
- `-0.624737*log(|v| + 1)`

Combining like terms:
- **v³**: `-0.0441723 + 0.333481 = 0.289309` → `0.289309*v³`
- **v**: `-0.333481 - 1.24947 = -1.58295` → `-1.58295*v`
- **x**: `-3.58221*x`
- **x*|v|^(1/3)**: `-0.17166*x*|v|^(1/3)`
- **log(|v|+1)**: `-0.624737*log(|v|+1)`

So GT = `0.289309*v³ - 1.58295*v - 3.58221*x - 0.17166*x*|v|^(1/3) - 0.624737*log(|v|+1)`

The basis functions in GT are: **{v³, v, x, x·|v|^(1/3), log(|v|+1)}** plus a possible constant (which is 0 here).

Now let me analyze each candidate. The key question for each is whether its basis functions can span exactly the GT's basis functions.

**Key observations about log terms:**
- `log(c*exp(c*v) + 1)` is a softplus-type function. For large negative v, it approaches 0; for large positive v, it approaches c*v. This is NOT equivalent to `log(|v|+1)` which is symmetric. **These are fundamentally different functions.**
- `log(c*|v| + 1)` can match `log(|v|+1)` with appropriate c.

**Key observations about polynomial terms:**
- `(c*|v| + 1)^4` expands to `c⁴|v|⁴ + 4c³|v|³ + 6c²|v|² + 4c|v| + 1`. This introduces |v|⁴, |v|³, |v|², |v|, and constant terms. Note |v|³ = v²·|v| ≠ v³.
- `(c*|v| + 1)^3` expands to `c³|v|³ + 3c²|v|² + 3c|v| + 1`.

The GT requires `v³` (an odd function) and `log(|v|+1)` (an even function). 

**Critical issue with softplus candidates (Candidates 1-13):**
`log(c*exp(c*v) + 1)` is NOT `log(|v|+1)`. The softplus is not symmetric in v. And `(c*|v|+1)^4` generates even-power-like terms (|v|^k), not v³.

Let me check which candidates have both `v³` (or can generate it) AND `log(|v|+1)`:

**Candidates using `log(c*exp(c*v)+1)` instead of `log(|v|+1)`:** These CANNOT match because softplus ≠ log(|v|+1). This eliminates Candidates 1-13.

**Candidates using `x*log(c*|v|+1)`:** This gives `x*log(|v|+1)` with appropriate c, but GT needs `log(|v|+1)` without x multiplied. These cannot produce a standalone `log(|v|+1)` term. This eliminates Candidates 14-26 (they have `x*log(c*|v|+1)` not `log(c*|v|+1)`).

Wait, let me re-examine. Candidates 14-26 have `x*log(c*|v|+1)` but GT needs `log(|v|+1)` (no x factor). These don't match.

**Candidates 27-50** use rational functions of |v| like `Abs(v)/(c+Abs(v))`, `v/(c+Abs(v))`, `x/(c+Abs(v))`. These are fundamentally different from `log(|v|+1)`. They cannot produce a logarithmic term.

**Candidates 36-42** use `exp(c*v)` and `(c*|v|+1)^3` and `v^c8 * x`. None have `log(|v|+1)`.

After careful analysis, **none of the candidates** contain the basis function `log(|v|+1)` (without x multiplication), which is required by the GT.

Candidate 1-50 verdict: [NO MATCH] for all.
